[2024-12-17, 14:55:47] Ola: STATE HOUSE PRESS RELEASE

PRESIDENT TINUBU APPROVES RECONSTITUTION OF NELMCO BOARD AND AMENDED STRUCTURE

President Bola Tinubu has approved the reconstitution of the Board of the Nigeria Electricity Liability Management Company (NELMCO) with a modification to the NELMCO Board structure, which empowers the Office of the Minister of Power to take over the Board Chairmanship from the Office of the Minister of Finance, in view of NELMCO's central role in the operation of the Nigeria Electricity Supply Industry (NESI).

Honourable Minister of Power — NELMCO Board Chairman

Honourable Minister of Finance — NELMCO Board Vice-Chairman

Director-General, Debt Management Office — Member

Director-General, Bureau of Public Enterprises — Member

Mrs. Mojoyinoluwa Dekalu-Thomas — NELMCO Managing Director/CEO (five-year term)

Mr. Joseph Asuku Bello — NELMCO Executive Director, Asset Management (five-year term)

Mr. Hassan Yahya — NELMCO Executive Director, Corporate Services (five-year term)

Mr. Abdullahi Mahmud Gaya — Non-Executive Director (three-year term)

Prof. (Mrs) Ayanfemi Ayandele — Non-Executive Director (three-year term)

In consonance with his Renewed Hope Agenda, President Tinubu anticipates that NELMCO Board's new structure and composition will yield expeditious and measurable progress in the management of the power sector's post-privatization liabilities to create conditions for the sustainable attainment of world-class standards of operational efficiency across all sub-components of the Nigeria Electricity Supply Industry (NESI).

Chief Ajuri Ngelale

Special Adviser to the President

(Media & Publicity)

[2025-03-14, 15:43:29] Makir: I just got off a call with Axxela, and here’s where we stand:

My Concern: Their financial model assumes an energy cost of 3.5 cents per kWh, whereas we modeled ours at 1.2 cents per kWh. That’s a big difference, and my concern is that investors will see 3.5 cents as too high, especially compared to what’s available in other regions.

My Reasoning: Since the gas being used is flared and stranded, it should be close to free—there’s no competition for it, so we shouldn’t be paying a premium.

Axxela’s Counterpoint: They factored in the gas turbine and its maintenance costs, which contribute to their higher energy price.

My Response: I understand that the turbine and maintenance are necessary expenses, but the actual gas price itself should still be lower given that it’s stranded and not being bid on by others.

Next Steps: We’re now looking at whether we can keep the all-in operational cost under 3 cents per kWh and still make this work. We are still looking to work together, but we need a stronger understanding of where the benefits lie in working with them at 3 cents, as that’s quite high compared to other locations.

[2025-07-03, 13:19:59] Ola: 🧾 Talking Points: Nigerian Subsidiary Structure for Foreign Partners

1. Purpose of the Nigerian Subsidiary

We are establishing a legally registered Nigerian subsidiary to:
	•	Serve as the local operating entity for all in-country activities.
	•	Allow us to apply for necessary licenses, permits, and regulatory approvals within Nigeria.
	•	Provide a legitimate local interface for our foreign partners to operate collaboratively under Nigerian law.

This structure allows us and our partners to engage in operations without each party needing to individually register a business in Nigeria.

2. Ownership and Control
	•	The subsidiary will be legally registered under a third-party nominee or local consultancy firm, meaning:
	•	The parent company will not be listed as a direct owner.
	•	This shields the parent from Nigerian tax, compliance, and operational exposure.
	•	The parent company and partners will retain commercial control via legal agreements (not shareholding).

3. Mining-as-a-Service (MaaS) Agreement
	•	A Mining-as-a-Service (MaaS) contract will define the relationship:
	•	The Nigerian subsidiary will act as a local operator and service provider.
	•	The parent company and international partners will own the miners, retain mining rewards, and direct operations remotely.
	•	The Nigerian entity will receive a service fee or management fee for hosting, maintaining, and facilitating regulatory compliance.

4. Use by International Partners
	•	International partners can:
	•	Deploy hardware (e.g. ASIC miners) under the subsidiary’s operational license.
	•	Avoid registering a local company themselves.
	•	Operate in Nigeria legally and transparently using our infrastructure.
	•	We’ll extend individual service agreements for each partner, tailored to their level of involvement.

5. Compliance and Tax
	•	The Nigerian entity will comply with all local regulations and tax obligations related to service provision.
	•	Since mining rewards are earned by the parent/partner companies outside Nigeria, they are not subject to Nigerian income tax.
	•	The structure ensures regulatory legitimacy while optimising tax efficiency.

6. Key Benefits for Everyone
	•	Simple entry into the Nigerian market without bureaucratic setup.
	•	Legal, local presence to apply for permits and contracts.
	•	Each partner retains control over their mining revenue and hardware.
	•	Transparent relationships defined through clear service contracts.

Let me know if you’d like a one-page PDF version or Word version of this for distribution.
